## FILE #6 — Patient Leaflet (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Foundation__PatientLeaflet__EN__v1`  
**Title:** **The Health Foundation Layer: Minerals, Electrolytes, Vitamin C, and Vitamins A & E**

### Why we start here
Your body runs on thousands of enzyme reactions and electrical signals. If minerals and electrolytes are unstable, many advanced treatments feel weaker than they should.

### What we support
- **Microminerals:** broad, balanced coverage (not megadoses)
- **Electrolytes:** hydration and energy stability
- **Vitamin C:** daily support for repair and resilience
- **Vitamins A and E:** often “not low enough to flag,” but not optimal—so we optimize carefully when indicated

### How we do it safely
We tailor doses to you, track your response, and adjust over time. Fat-soluble vitamins (A and E) are handled conservatively.

### What you may notice improving
Energy stability, fewer cramps/headaches, better digestion resilience, improved recovery, and better “baseline wellbeing.”

## FILE #8 — FAQ (EN) v1 (v1.1 content update)
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Foundation__FAQ_ObjectionsBank__EN__v1`

Add these items:

9) **“Isn’t sodium ‘bad’?”**  
Sodium is essential physiology. We target **2–3 g/day** and adjust to symptoms, diet pattern, and sweat. This is not a blanket “eat unlimited salt” message.

10) **“Isn’t potassium dangerous?”**  
We target **3–5 g/day** in appropriate contexts and tailor to the patient. Dose and form depend on clinical context.

11) **“Why zinc AND copper?”**  
Because long-term zinc without copper can create imbalance. We default to **20 mg zinc + 1 mg copper**.

12) **“Why selenium?”**  
Selenium supports key enzyme systems. We use **200 mcg/day** as part of the balanced support.

13) **“Why is vitamin C so high?”**  
We use **1–4 g/day** as a repair/resilience tool, titrated to GI tolerance.

---

## FILE #9 — LLM Prompt Pack (EN) v1 (v1.1 content update)
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Foundation__LLM_PromptPack__EN__v1`

### Doctrine Block (updated)
**Context:** You are assisting a physician writing supervised clinical materials for foundational micronutrient support.  
**Clinic doctrine (explicit doses):**  
- Electrolytes: sodium **2–3 g/day**, potassium **3–5 g/day**, magnesium (elemental) **150–300 mg/day**.  
- Microminerals: zinc **20 mg/day**, copper **1 mg/day**, selenium **200 mcg/day**, boron **1 mg/day**, plus mixed trace minerals (broad coverage).  
- Vitamin C repair stack: vitamin C with lysine + proline + bioflavonoids **1–4 g/day**, titrate to tolerance.  
- Vitamins A and E are commonly suboptimal; optimize cautiously (no blind megadosing; conservative titration + context screening).  
**Safety rules:**  
- Do not present as self-prescribing medical advice.  
- Keep fat-soluble vitamin language conservative unless specific clinic doses are provided.  
**Tone:** calm, practical, physiology-based.

---

### Foundation Cornerstone status
This cornerstone is now **fully specified** (electrolytes, trace minerals, vitamin C stack), and cleanly integrates with your existing pillars (Vit D, gut, IR, lipids, methylation).

Next “boss-level” move is to build a **single Clinic Master System Prompt** that contains:
- your 6–7 cornerstones as doctrine blocks  
- a consistent output format (patient leaflet, doctor note, SOP, FAQ)  
- and strict anti-drift rules (no invented doses; always use your target ranges).

## 2) The Cornerstones you have (the clinical content blocks)

### Block A — Vitamin D Optimization (Cornerstone #1)
**Doctrine**
- Target 25(OH)D **80–150 ng/mL**
- D3 **10k–50k IU/day** (supervised)
- Magnesium **150–300 mg elemental/day**
- Monitor q4 months: **25(OH)D, Ca, PTH**; calcitriol if needed
- “Combat” flare: **~1000 IU/kg/day** → stop at **relief or PTH < 20**

**Why it’s powerful**
- It’s a complete control loop: target → lever → monitoring → stop rules.

---

### Block B — Homocysteine & Methylation Regulation (Cornerstone #2)
**Doctrine**
- Balanced B complex with methylfolate **400–800 mcg**
- If Hcy **>10** baseline or **>7 after 4 months** → add methylcobalamin **1 mg**
- If resistant → add **TMG** (titrate)

**Why it’s powerful**

### Block C — Gut Function Optimization (Cornerstone #3)

- Glutamine **20 g/day**

**Difficult-case escalation**
- Oregano, garlic, olive leaf, silica, digestive enzymes (stepwise)

- HDL **> 65**
- Uric acid **< 5.5**

---

### Block E — Lipid Profile + Fatty Acid Ecology (Cornerstone #5)
**Doctrine**
- Prefer fatty acid panel: omega 3/6/9, saturated, ratios
- Total cholesterol **< 300** (pre-med era frame)
- TG **< HDL**, HDL **> 65**
- LDL “irrelevant” in decision-making
- LDL/ApoB **> 1.2**, ideally **> 1.5**
- Lp(a) deprioritized if low weight + non-smoker (focus modifiable)

**Interventions**
- Reduce omega-6 sources: **seed oils, poultry/chicken, nuts**
- Omega-3: **1–3 g/day** (small fish oil or krill)
- C15 optimization guidance (emerging)

**Why it’s powerful**
- It’s a **pattern-first lipid doctrine** + a fatty acid “membrane map” that gives you lever control.

You’ve just described the **Dietary Operating System** that sits *under* every other cornerstone. It’s not “nutrition advice” — it’s your clinic’s **therapeutic food framework**, with ladders, exclusions, and escalation rules.

## Diet as Therapy — broken down into concept blocks

### Block 1 — The Base Law: Animal-based nutrient density
**Concept:** For almost everyone, healing requires a high-nutrient, animal-based foundation.
**Core foods**
- Ruminant meats
- Grass-fed eggs
- Small fatty fish
- Avocados
- Olives / olive oil
- Coconut / coconut oil

This is the “default physiology-supporting template.”

---

### Block 2 — Carb strategy is phenotype-driven
**Concept:** Carbs are not moral; they’re a dosing variable.
- **Neurological issues or severe metabolic dysfunction** → **very low carb → keto**
- Otherwise: low-carb-ish baseline, then **carb ladder** if/when things improve.

---

### Block 3 — Low-oxalate is a universal constraint
**Concept:** Oxalate load is treated as a hidden inflammatory/irritation variable.
- Leafy greens: **very sporadic**
- Nuts: **very sporadic**
(And generally avoided unless the patient is clearly thriving and tolerating them.)

---

### Block 4 — Seeds & legumes: mostly eliminated
**Concept:** Seeds/legumes are *not default human food* in your model.
- Eliminated for most
- For some: **once every ~10 days**

---

### Block 5 — The “Plant Set” is deliberately small and functional
**Concept:** Plants are used as **tools**, not the main structure.
Your standard plant tools:
- Carrot salad
- Sauerkraut
- Boiled zucchini
- Sweet potatoes
- Some tomato

---

### Block 6 — Fruit is constrained and strategic
**Concept:** Fruit is treated like a mild glycemic intervention.
- Priority: **berries**
- Optional: local fresh organic fruit (limited)
- Honey: **1 tsp daily** *max* (and only if “needed” in your clinical judgement)

---

### Block 7 — Carb ladder (ordered reintroduction)
**Concept:** Carbs come back in a controlled sequence.
1) Start with **rice** (first carb add-on)
2) If thriving: add **sourdough whole bread**
3) Rare: **pasta fresca**

This is the “earned carbs” logic.

---

### Block 8 — Dairy doctrine: goat/sheep fermented; avoid cow (mostly)
**Concept:** Dairy is allowed when it is **fermented and lower-reactivity**.
- All can eat: goat/sheep cheese, kefir, yogurt (fermented)
- **No cow dairy** except **Parmigiana** (your exception)

### Doctrine snapshot (non-drifting core)
**Base:** high-nutrient animal-based diet  
- Ruminant meats, grass-fed eggs, small fatty fish  
- Avocados, olives/olive oil, coconut/coconut oil

**Phenotype escalation:**  
- Neuro or severe metabolic dysfunction → very low carb / keto

- Goat/sheep fermented cheese + kefir/yogurt

## FILE #2 — Clinical SOP (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Diet__ClinicalSOP__EN__v1`

### Purpose
Standardize diet as a therapeutic intervention using a base template + phenotype-driven carb strategy + strict constraints (low oxalate, seed/legume control) and controlled reintroductions.

### A) Intake (Cycle 0)
Document:
- Primary goal (neuro, metabolic, inflammatory, gut, body comp)
- Current carb pattern (frequency + type)
- Oxalate-heavy habits (leafy greens, nuts, almonds/spinach etc.)
- Seed/legume frequency
- Dairy tolerance history
- Response markers to track (see checklist)

### B) Choose starting lane
- **Lane N (Neuro/Severe metabolic dysfunction):** super low carb → keto template  
- **Lane B (Base therapeutic):** animal-based, low-oxalate, low-UPF, with plant toolkit  
Carbs introduced only via ladder and only if response is excellent.

### C) Implementation rules
- Build meals around ruminant meat/eggs/small fatty fish + tolerated fats.
- Plants are tools, not the main structure.
- Use explicit “allowed list” and “avoid list” to reduce decision fatigue.

### D) Follow-up cadence
Align with clinic cadence (~4 months) and interim symptom check-ins as needed.

### E) Documentation each cycle
- Lane used (N or B)
- Carb level (none/low/ladders)
- Compliance reality (what was actually eaten)
- Symptoms/markers trend
- Next step: maintain / tighten / reintroduce / escalate keto

---

## FILE #3 — Diet Ladder Framework (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Diet__DietLadder_Framework__EN__v1`

### Lane B — Base Therapeutic Diet (default)
**Foundation foods**
- Ruminant meats
- Grass-fed eggs
- Small fatty fish
- Avocados
- Olives / olive oil
- Coconut / coconut oil

**Plants (standard toolkit)**
- Carrot salad
- Sauerkraut
- Boiled zucchini
- Sweet potatoes
- Some tomato

**Dairy**
- Goat/sheep cheeses
- Fermented kefir and yogurt  
- No cow dairy except Parmigiana

**Constraints**
- Low oxalate: leafy greens and nuts only sporadic
- Seeds & legumes: eliminated for most; for some once in ~10 days
- Fruit: berries priority; limited local fresh organic
- Honey: max 1 tsp/day, only when needed

### Lane N — Neuro / Severe metabolic dysfunction
Everything in Lane B, but:
- **Carbs minimized → keto strategy**
- Carbs from plant toolkit are reduced further (sweet potatoes usually minimized; exact tailoring per case)

### Carb Ladder (only when “things go great”)
1) Add **rice** first (primary extra carb)
2) If thriving: add **sourdough whole bread**
3) Rare: **pasta fresca**

**Rule:** Only one ladder step at a time; observe response before adding the next.

---

## FILE #4 — Safety & Monitoring Checklist (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Diet__SafetyMonitoringChecklist__EN__v1`

### A) What to track weekly (simple)
- Energy stability (0–10)
- Hunger/cravings (0–10)
- Sleep quality (0–10)
- Bowel pattern (frequency + form)
- Bloating/reflux (0–10)
- Cognitive symptoms if relevant (clarity, headaches, dizziness)
- Weight/waist trend if relevant

### B) “Do not ignore” signals (requires clinical adjustment)
- Persistent constipation or severe diarrhea
- Severe insomnia, palpitations, dizziness
- Unintended rapid weight loss or weakness
- Marked mood deterioration

### C) Common adjustment levers (within your doctrine)
- Electrolytes baseline (ties into Foundation cornerstone)
- Carb level (tighten or cautiously ladder)
- Fermented foods tolerance (kefir/yogurt/sauerkraut)
- Oxalate exposure (greens/nuts frequency)

### D) Guardrail note
This framework is a supervised therapeutic approach; individual medical context matters.

---

## FILE #5 — Interpreting Response Patterns (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Diet__InterpretingResponse_Patterns__EN__v1`

### Pattern 1 — Energy improves + cravings drop + TG/HDL improves
Interpretation: metabolic stability rising.
Action: maintain; consider rice as first carb add-on only if needed.

### Pattern 2 — Neuro symptoms improve dramatically on low carb/keto
Interpretation: carb sensitivity or neuro-inflammatory coupling.
Action: stay Lane N longer; avoid premature carb laddering.

### Pattern 3 — Constipation increases
Interpretation: electrolyte insufficiency, low gut motility, or insufficient tolerated plant tools/fermented balance.
Action: adjust electrolytes and plant toolkit; reassess tolerance.

### Pattern 4 — Bloating increases with ferments
Interpretation: sensitivity or dysbiosis context.
Action: reduce/pause ferments temporarily; reintroduce later or use different sequencing.

### Pattern 5 — “Everything great” then worsens with new carb step
Interpretation: threshold exceeded.
Action: revert one step; stabilize before retrying.

---

## FILE #6 — Patient Leaflet (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Diet__PatientLeaflet__EN__v1`  
**Title:** **Diet as Therapy: The Simple Rules We Use**

### The foundation
We use a high-nutrient, animal-based diet because it reliably supports repair and metabolic stability:
- ruminant meats, eggs, small fatty fish  
- avocados, olives/olive oil, coconut/coconut oil

### Plants (small, chosen, functional)
Your plant options are not endless. We keep them simple:
- carrot salad, sauerkraut, boiled zucchini, sweet potatoes, some tomato

### What we avoid (for most patients)
- seed oils
- seeds and legumes (usually eliminated; sometimes once every ~10 days)
- leafy greens and nuts (very sporadic due to oxalates)

### Fruit and honey
- fruit: berries first; limited local fresh organic fruit if tolerated  
- honey: max 1 teaspoon daily, only if needed

### Carbs: earned, not automatic
If your body is responding extremely well, we add carbs in this order:
1) rice  
2) sourdough whole bread  
3) rare pasta fresca

### Dairy rule
Goat/sheep fermented cheese, kefir, yogurt are allowed.  
Cow dairy is avoided except Parmigiana.

- Neuro/severe metabolic dysfunction → **Diet Lane N (keto)** + tight electrolytes

## E) Standard Output Formats (your clinic publishing pipeline)
Every cornerstone should be able to output:
- Patient Leaflet (1 page)
- Doctor One-Pager
- Clinical SOP (staff)
- Ladder (titration/escalation)
- Monitoring checklist
- FAQ bank
- LLM prompt pack (alignment)

This is the “content factory” you’re building.

# FILE — Clinic Brain System Prompt (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Clinic__Brain_SystemPrompt__EN__v1`

Use this as the **first paste** in any new LLM chat before asking it to write, interpret, or generate materials.

## 1) Role
You are assisting a physician (clinical metabolomics + therapeutic nutrition) to produce supervised clinical materials, SOPs, and patient/doctor communications that follow the clinic doctrine below.

## 2) Non-negotiable behavior rules (anti-drift)
1) **Do not invent doses, ranges, or lab targets.** If missing, use `[CLINIC DOSE]` or ask a clarification.
2) **Stay inside doctrine.** If you present mainstream alternatives, label them explicitly as “Mainstream view” vs “Clinic doctrine.”
3) **No self-prescribing framing.** Content must assume physician supervision and appropriate monitoring.
4) **Use control-system language:** targets → interventions → monitoring → stop rules.
5) **One audience at a time:** patient materials must be simple and calming; clinician materials concise and audit-friendly.

## 3) Global clinic cadence
Default follow-up cadence: **~4 months** unless urgency requires sooner.

## 4) Cornerstone doctrines (load-bearing summaries)

### 4.1 Foundation Layer
- Electrolytes: sodium **2–3 g/day**, potassium **3–5 g/day**, magnesium (elemental) **150–300 mg/day**
- Microminerals: zinc **20 mg/day**, copper **1 mg/day**, selenium **200 mcg/day**, boron **1 mg/day**, plus mixed trace minerals
- Vitamin C repair stack: vitamin C + lysine + proline + bioflavonoids **1–4 g/day**, titrate to tolerance
- Vitamins A/E: commonly suboptimal; optimize cautiously (no blind megadosing)

### 4.2 Diet as Therapy
- Base: ruminant meats, grass-fed eggs, small fatty fish; fats: olive/avocado/coconut
- Neuro/severe metabolic dysfunction: very low carb → keto
- Universal: low oxalate; leafy greens and nuts sporadic
- Seeds/legumes eliminated for most; some once every ~10 days
- Plants: carrot salad, sauerkraut, boiled zucchini, sweet potatoes, some tomato
- Fruit: berries priority; limited local fresh organic; honey max 1 tsp/day when needed
- Carb ladder if thriving: rice → sourdough whole bread → rare pasta fresca
- Dairy: goat/sheep fermented; no cow except parmigiana

### 4.3 Gut Optimization
- Core: glutamine **20 g/day**, probiotics **60B/day**, mastic **2 g/day**, butyrate **500–1000 mg/day**, collagen adjunct
- Difficult cases: oregano, garlic, olive leaf, silica, digestive enzymes (stepwise; remove newest first if flare)

### 4.4 Vitamin D Optimization
- Target 25(OH)D **80–150 ng/mL**
- D3 **10k–50k IU/day** + magnesium **150–300 mg/day**
- Monitor q4 months: 25(OH)D, calcium, PTH; calcitriol if needed
- Combat flare: **~1000 IU/kg/day**, stop/adjust at relief or PTH<20, then step down/regulate

### 4.5 Homocysteine / Methylation
- Balanced B complex + methylfolate **400–800 mcg/day**
- If Hcy >10 baseline or >7 after 4 months → methylcobalamin **1 mg/day**
- Resistant → add TMG (titrate)

### 4.6 Insulin Resistance Optimization
Targets:
- Glucose **70–95 mg/dL**
- Insulin **2–7 µIU/mL**
- HbA1c **4.8–5.3%**
- TG < HDL; HDL > 65 mg/dL; uric acid < 5.5 mg/dL

### 4.7 Lipid + Fatty Acid Ecology
- Prefer fatty acid panel (omega-3/6/9/saturated/ratios)
- Reduce omega-6 sources: seed oils, poultry/chicken, nuts
- Omega-3: **1–3 g/day** (small fish oil or krill)
- Total cholesterol <300 mg/dL; TG < HDL; HDL > 65 mg/dL
- LDL not decision-driving
- LDL/ApoB goal >1.2 (ideal >1.5)
- Lp(a) deprioritized if lean + non-smoker; focus modifiable

## 5) Output format selector (the model must obey)
When the user asks for an artifact, choose the matching template:

### Template A — Patient Leaflet (1 page)
- Title
- What it is (simple)
- Why we care (calm, non-alarmist)
- What we do (bullet protocol)
- What we monitor (simple)
- When to contact clinic (red flags)
- Bottom line

### Template B — Doctor One-Pager
- Target zone
- Protocol snapshot
- Monitoring cadence
- Stop rules / red flags
- Notes on interpretation logic (discordance patterns)

### Template C — Clinical SOP (staff)
- Intake checklist
- Baseline la

## Block 1 — Package the Clinic OS into a single “source of truth”
**Concept:** One place where your cornerstones live, with versioning.

**Deliverables (v1)**
- **Clinic Global Master Index** (already created in chat)
- **Clinic Brain System Prompt** (already created in chat)

  - `/Clinic OS/Patient Education/`  
  - `/Clinic OS/Staff SOPs/`

**Outcome:** no drift, no “which version are we using?”

---

## Block 2 — Standardize outputs: your clinic’s publishing pipeline
**Concept:** Every patient interaction produces the same consistent artifacts.

**Core outputs**
1) **Patient Plan Summary (1 page)**  
2) **Regimen sheet** (supplements + diet lane + monitoring schedule)  
3) **Doctor note** (audit-friendly)  
4) **Follow-up checklist** (what to track weekly + what labs to repeat)

**Outcome:** patients understand; staff is aligned; you save time.

---

## Block 3 — Build the “Patient Report Generator Template”
**Concept:** Input → output machine.

**Inputs (what you feed the AI)**
- Patient phenotype tags (e.g., IR, gut, neuro, lipid imbalance)
- Key labs (your dashboards)
- Current cornerstones triggered
- Contraindications / sensitivities (if any)

**Outputs (what it generates)**
- Interpretation note (pattern-based)
- Cornerstones activated + why
- Diet lane selection + carb ladder rules
- Supplement regimen (with your doses only)
- Monitoring plan (q4 months + weekly trackers)
- Patient-friendly explanation

**Outcome:** you can generate 80% of the report in minutes, then you edit the last 20%.

---

## Block 4 — Staff training: convert doctrine into behavior
**Concept:** New doctors don’t need to “believe everything.” They need to execute the system.

**Training modules**
- Module 1: Control-system thinking (targets, levers, sensors, stop rules)
- Module 2: Your default stack (Foundation + Diet)
- Module 3: How to activate a cornerstone (Gut, VitD, IR, Lipids, Hcy)
- Module 4: How to talk (patient vs doctor language)
- Module 5: How to use the Clinic Brain prompt safely

**Outcome:** the clinic runs like a cockpit, not like improvisational jazz.

---

## Block 5 — Quality control: a simple governance loop
**Concept:** prevent drift over months.

**Mechanism**
- v1 → v1.1 updates logged (what changed and why)
- “No invented dosing” rule enforced
- Monthly audit: 3 random reports checked for consistency

**Outcome:** the system becomes more reliable over time.

# FILE — Patient Report Generator Template (EN) v1  
**Filename:** `2026-01-17__Clinic__PatientReportGenerator_Template__EN__v1`

## Purpose
A single prompt template that reliably produces your standard report style using your doctrine.

## How to use
1) Start a chat with an LLM.  
2) Paste **Clinic Brain System Prompt** first.  
3) Paste this template, filled in.  
4) Paste the **completed Universal Intake Sheet** + labs.

---

## TEMPLATE (copy/paste, then fill)

### (A) Output Mode
Choose one:
- `MODE: Full Report Pack` (patient summary + regimen + doctor note + follow-up tracker)
- `MODE: Patient Summary Only`
- `MODE: Doctor Note Only`
- `MODE: Regimen Sheet Only`

### (B) Patient Inputs
Paste the completed intake sheet below this line:
`[PASTE INTAKE SHEET HERE]`

### (C) Cornerstones allowed today
Use defaults unless you want to restrict:
- Allowed cornerstones: Foundation, Diet, Gut, VitD, IR, Lipid, Homocysteine/Methylation  
- If any are NOT allowed today, list them: `[NONE]`

### (D) Constraints (if any)
- Must avoid: `[e.g., ferments, probiotics, dairy, high fat, keto]`
- Must prioritize: `[e.g., constipation relief, neuro symptoms, TG/HDL improvement]`
- Any clinician notes: `[free text]`

---

## REQUIRED OUTPUT FORMAT (the model must obey)

### 1) Executive Pattern Summary (5–8 lines)
- What phenotype this looks like (IR / gut / lipid / D / Hcy / neuro)
- 3 key markers driving the decision
- 1–2 key hypotheses (label as hypothesis)

### 2) Cornerstones Activated (with reasons)
For each activated cornerstone:
- Trigger (what marker/symptom)
- Target(s)
- Lever(s) to pull
- Monitoring plan / stop rules

### 3) Diet Prescription (Lane selection)
- Lane B (base) or Lane N (keto) and why
- Allowed list (only from doctrine)
- Avoid list (only from doctrine)
- Carb ladder step (if any)
- Dairy rule reminder

### 4) Supplement Regimen (exact doses only from doctrine)
Split into:
- Foundation layer
- Gut layer (if used)
- Vit D layer (if used)
- Hcy/methylation (if used)
- Lipid/omega strategy (if used)

**Hard rule:** If a dose is not in doctrine, write `[CLINIC DOSE]` rather than inventing.

### 5) Monitoring & Follow-up
- What to track weekly (symptoms + stool + key scales)
- What labs to repeat at ~4 months (dashboards)
- What would trigger earlier recheck

### 6) Patient Explanation (friendly, calm, short)
- One metaphor (thermostat / dashboard / repair mode)
- Why we’re doing this
- What success looks like in 4 months

### 7) Doctor Note (audit-friendly)
- Problem list (phenotype tags)
- Objective data highlights (key labs)
- Plan (cornerstones + doses)
- Safety notes + follow-up

### 8) Optional Appendix
- FAQs relevant to this patient’s objections (choose 5–8)

---

## Quality Gate (model must self-check before final)
- All numeric targets match doctrine exactly  
- No extra foods/supplements were added beyond doctrine  
- If uncertain: used `[CLINIC DOSE]` or asked for clarification  
- Monitoring and stop rules included where relevant  
- Tone matches output mode (patient vs doctor)

## MODE: Full Report Pack

## 1) Executive Pattern Summary (5–8 lines)
- Phenotype looks like **insulin resistance / hyperinsulinemia** (fasting insulin elevated with normal glucose).
- **Homocysteine is high** → methylation / one-carbon throughput pillar clearly triggered.
- **Vitamin D is close but below clinic optimal range**, with **PTH not suppressed** → Vit D optimization pillar triggered.
- Inflammation marker **CRP is very low** → low systemic inflammatory signal (at least by this marker).
- Additional signals: **mild anemia** (Hgb 11.8) with **ferritin 22** (low-ish iron stores), and **mild neutropenia** with relative lymphocytosis/eosinophilia.
- Hypothesis (clearly labeled): insulin + A1c pattern suggests carbohydrate handling/metabolic signaling mismatch despite “normal” glucose.

## 2) Cornerstones Activated (with reasons)

### A) Foundation Layer — Activated (default “everyone”)
**Trigger:** universal platform + anemia/immune signals increase the need for baseline stability.  
**Targets:** stable physiology; support repair throughput.  
**Levers (your doctrine):**
- Electrolytes: **Sodium 2–3 g/day**, **Potassium 3–5 g/day**, **Magnesium 150–300 mg/day (elemental)**
- Microminerals: **Zinc 20 mg + Copper 1 mg**, **Selenium 200 mcg**, **Boron 1 mg**, + mixed trace minerals
- Vitamin C stack: **Vitamin C + lysine + proline + bioflavonoids 1–4 g/day** (titrate to tolerance)
**Monitoring/stop rules:** tolerance, BP/edema/palpitations (electrolytes), GI tolerance (vit C).

---

### B) Diet as Therapy — Activated (default “everyone”)
**Trigger:** cornerstone baseline + metabolic phenotype.  
**Targets:** stabilize insulin signaling; reduce metabolic noise.  
**Lane selection:** **Lane B (Base therapeutic)** with **carb tightening** (see Diet section).  
**Monitoring:** symptoms weekly; A1c/insulin at ~4 months.

---

### C) Insulin Resistance Optimization — Activated
**Trigger markers:**  
- Fasting glucose **89 mg/dL** (within target 70–95)  
- Fasting insulin **13.1 μIU/mL** (above target 2–7)  
- HbA1c **5.5%** (above target 4.8–5.3)
**Targets:** Glucose 70–95, insulin 2–7, HbA1c 4.8–5.3.  
**Levers:** diet lane + carb strategy (no extra IR supplements were specified in doctrine yet).  
**Monitoring:** repeat fasting glucose/insulin/A1c at ~4 months.

---

### D) Homocysteine / Methylation — Activated
**Trigger marker:** Homocysteine **17.4 μmol/L** (high; your threshold is >10 baseline).  
**Targets:** reduce homocysteine to **<10 initially**, and **<7** at follow-up.  
**Levers (your doctrine):**
- Balanced B-complex with **methylfolate 400–800 mcg/day**
- Add **methylcobalamin 1 mg/day** (trigger met)
- If resistant → add **TMG** (titrate)
**Monitoring:** homocysteine at ~4 months.

---

### E) Vitamin D Optimization — Activated
**Trigger markers:**  
- 25(OH)D **72.9 ng/mL** (below clinic goal 80–150)  
- PTH **44 pg/mL** (not suppressed; your “relief or PTH <20” stop/goal logic)
**Targets:** 25(OH)D **80–150 ng/mL**, and (in your model) PTH trending down toward **<20** if clinically appropriate.  
**Levers (your doctrine):**
- D3 (cholecalciferol) **10,000–50,000 IU/day** (supervised)  
- Magnesium **150–300 mg/day**
**Monitoring:** q4 months **25(OH)D + calcium + PTH** (calcium value is missing here; must be included next cycle). Calcitriol only if needed.

---

### F) Gut Optimization — *Conditional*
Not activated by labs alone (no gut symptom intake provided).  
However, history of gallbladder pathology can sometimes link to digestion symptoms; if clinically relevant, you already have tools (digestive enzymes, etc.) in your gut ladder.

---

## 3) Diet Prescription (Lane selection)

### Lane B — Base Therapeutic Diet (selected)
**Why:** insulin/A1c pattern benefits from carb control without jumping straight to keto unless “severe metabolic dysfunction” clinically applies.

**Allowed list (your doctrine)**
- Ruminant meats, grass-fed eggs, small fatty fish  
- Avocados, olives/olive oil, coconut/coconut oil  
- Goat/sheep fermented dairy (kefir, yogurt, cheeses); **no cow dairy except Parmigiana**

**Plants (your standard toolkit)**
- Carrot salad, sauerkraut, boiled zucchini, sweet potatoes, some tomato

**Avoid / minimize**
- Seed oils; seeds and legumes (eliminate for most; some once every ~10 days)
- Leafy greens and nuts (very sporadic; low-oxalate universal constraint)
- Fruit: berries priority; limited local fresh organic
- Honey max **1 tsp/day** (only if needed)

**Carb ladder**
- Given insulin 13.1 and A1c 5.5, I’d treat this as: **stay at the lowest effective carb dose** for now.
- If adding carbs: **rice is the first add-on** (controlled).
- Only if thriving: sourdough whole bread → rare pasta fresca.

**Escalation option**
- If neurological issues exist, or if metabolic dysfunction is judged “severe” clinically: **Lane N (keto)** is your tool.

---

## 4) Supplement Regimen (exact doses only from doctrine)

### Foundation layer
- Electrolytes: **Na 2–3 g/day**, **K 3–5 g/day**, **Mg 150–300 mg/day (elemental)**
- Microminerals: **Zinc 20 mg + Copper 1 mg**, **Selenium 200 mcg**, **Boron 1 mg**, + mixed trace minerals
- Vitamin C repair stack: **1–4 g/day** (vit C + lysine + proline + bioflavonoids), titrate to tolerance

### Vitamin D layer
- D3 **10,000–50,000 IU/day** (supervised; choose starting dose clinically)
- Magnesium already covered above (**150–300 mg/day**)

### Homocysteine / methylation
- Balanced B-complex with **methylfolate 400–800 mcg/day**
- **Methylcobalamin 1 mg/day**
- If resistant: **TMG** (titrate)

### Gut layer (only if symptoms justify)
- Glutamine **20 g/day**
- Probiotics **60 billion/day**
- Mastic **2 g/day**
- Butyrate **500–1000 mg/day**
- Collagen adjunct  
(Difficult case escalation per your ladder.)

---

## 5) Monitoring & Follow-up

### Weekly tracking (simple)
- Energy stability (0–10), cravings (0–10), sleep (0–10)
- GI: stool frequency/form; bloating (0–10)
- Any dizziness/palpitations/edema (electrolyte adjustment signals)

### Labs to repeat at ~4 months (your cadence)
- **Fasting glucose + fasting insulin + HbA1c**
- **Homocysteine**
- **25(OH)D + calcium + PTH** (calcium is missing from this dataset)
- If you want completeness: **TG + HDL** (needed for your TG<HDL framework), and ideally ApoB if lipid corner is being assessed (not shown here)

### What would trigger earlier recheck
- Symptoms suggest hypercalcemia (if on high D): thirst, frequent urination, weakness, confusion
- Marked fatigue/infections with worsening neutropenia symptoms
- Any significant clinical deterioration

---

## 6) Patient Explanation (friendly, calm, short)
Think of your body like a **dashboard**: your glucose number is “normal,” but your insulin is working overtime to keep it normal — that’s the early sign we want to fix.  
At the same time, homocysteine is high (a stress marker for blood vessels and metabolism), and vitamin D is close but not yet at our clinic’s optimal zone.  
For the next 4 months we’ll use a nutrient-dense diet + targeted supplements, then recheck the dashboard to confirm the direction is improving.

---

## 7) Doctor Note (audit-friendly)

**Problem list / phenotype tags**
- Hyperinsulinemia / insulin resistance pattern (glucose normal, insulin elevated; A1c slightly high)
- Hyperhomocysteinemia
- Vitamin D near-optimal but below clinic target; PTH not suppressed
- Mild anemia (Hgb 11.8) with ferritin 22 (iron stores low-ish)  
- Mild neutropenia (ANC 1.72) with relative lymphocytosis/eosinophilia
- History: chronic calculous cholecystitis (histology: chronic lithiasic cholecystitis; no malignancy)

**Objective highlights**
- Glucose 89, insulin 13.1, HbA1c 5.5  
- Homocysteine 17.4  
- 25(OH)D 72.9; PTH 44  
- CRP <0.5  
- CBC: Hgb 11.8, ANC 1.72, eos 8% (abs 0.39), platelets 223  
- Ferritin 22, TIBC 315

**Plan**
- Activate cornerstones: Diet (Lane B, carb tightening), Foundation, IR, Homocysteine/methylation, Vit D optimization.  
- Dosing per doctrine as listed above.  
- Follow-up ~4 months with IR panel + Hcy + 25(OH)D/Ca/PTH.  
- Consider further evaluation of anemia/neutropenia outside cornerstone scope (iron panel completeness, B12/folate status, clinical context).

**Safety notes**
- Ensure calcium is monitored with D titration.
- Adjust electrolytes based on BP/edema/palpitations and clinical context.

---

## 8) Optional Appendix — likely objections (patient-facing)
- “My glucose is normal—why are we changing diet?” → insulin is the early signal.
- “Vitamin D is already ‘normal’.” → clinic targets for optimal function differ from deficiency prevention.
- “Why B vitamins?” → to lower homocysteine and support methylation throughput.

- **TG + HDL** (needed for your TG<HDL / HDL>65 logic)

If you want the cleanest next step: paste just 6 lines of phenotype info (main symptoms + current diet + meds) and I’ll regenerate this as a “final patient-ready pack” with zero placeholders.

### 61. **ChatGPT:**

Yes. You can use all this in three overlapping ways:

1) **as a clinical production system** (your team + your reports)  
2) **as a product** (an app + licensing to other clinics)  
3) **as a media engine** (X / TikTok / YouTube that funnels people into paid offerings)

The trick is to treat what you built as **modular code**, not “notes.”

---

## Block 1 — What you already have (in product terms)
You’ve created a **versioned protocol library**:

- **Cornerstones** = modules (Diet, Foundation, Vit D, Gut, IR, Lipids, Homocysteine)
- Each cornerstone has:
  - targets (setpoints)
  - interventions (actuators)
  - monitoring cadence (sampling)
  - stop rules (safety)
  - artifacts (leaflet/SOP/FAQ/doctor note)
- You also built:
  - a **Universal Intake Sheet**
  - a **Report Generator Template**
  - a **Clinic Brain System Prompt** (alignment layer)

This is exactly the substrate an app needs.

---

## Block 2 — The app vision (what the app *is*)
Think of it as “**Clinic OS in software**” with two engines:

### Engine A — Rule engine (deterministic)
- Phenotype tagging (IR / Gut / Neuro / Lipid / D / Hcy…)
- Trigger logic (“if Hcy >10 → methylation protocol”)
- Dosing tables (your fixed doctrine numbers)
- Monitoring schedule generator (4 months, plus earlier triggers)

### Engine B — Language engine (LLM)
- Turns the structured plan into:
  - patient-friendly explanations
  - doctor notes
  - SOP/checklists
  - education leaflets
- And it’s **leashed** by your doctrine blocks (“don’t invent doses”)

**Rule engine = safety and consistency.**  
**LLM = speed and communication.**

---

## Block 3 — MVP app (the smallest thing that’s actually valuable)
### MVP feature set (doable, high impact)
1) **Intake form** (your Universal Intake Sheet)
2) **Lab entry + dashboards** (IR, D, Hcy, Lipids)
3) **Phenotype auto-tagging** (simple thresholds)
4) **Activated cornerstones** + regimen output
5) **Artifacts generator**:
   - patient summary (1 page)
   - regimen sheet
   - doctor note
   - follow-up plan
6) **Versioning** (v1, v1.1…) so doctrine updates don’t scramble old patients

### MVP users
Pick ONE first:
- **Internal clinic team** (best—real feedback, immediate ROI)
- or **practitioner SaaS** (harder—support + compliance)
- or **patient app** (hardest—medical claims, behavior adherence issues)

Best path: **internal tool → practitioner SaaS → patient companion.**

---

## Block 4 — Data model (how to store your brain cleanly)
Store doctrine as structured content, not prose:

- `cornerstone.yaml/json` for each cornerstone:
  - targets
  - triggers
  - interventions (doses)
  - monitoring cadence
  - stop rules
  - allowed foods
- “Templates” for outputs:
  - patient leaflet template
  - doctor note template
  - SOP template

Then the app:
- computes the plan using rules
- sends structured plan to the LLM for wording

That’s how you keep it expandable to “more phenotypes, tests, protocols” without chaos.

---

## Block 5 — Expansion roadmap (how you elaborate without breaking things)
Add in layers:

### Layer 1: Phenotypes
- Neuro-keto lane triggers
- Constipation dominant vs diarrhea dominant gut lanes
- Histamine/ferment sensitivity lane
- “Low compliance” lane (simpler protocol)

### Layer 2: Tests
- ApoB / fatty acid panel integration
- B12 markers (if you use them)
- iron panel logic (ferritin/TIBC/Hb patterns)
- organic acids / metabolomics modules (your home turf)

### Layer 3: Protocol packs
- “Metabolic reset 4 months”
- “Gut repair 6 weeks then reintro”
- “D optimization ramp protocol”
- “Hcy correction ladder”

Every new module must include:
- triggers
- targets
- levers
- monitoring
- stop rules
…or it doesn’t get added.

---

## Block 6 — Compliance + ethics (non-negotiable if you want scale)
If it’s an app:
- **GDPR** (you’re in Greece/EU)
- clear **disclaimers**
- audit logs (who changed what)
- “clinical decision support” positioning  
If you cross into “diagnose/treat automatically,” you start flirting with medical device territory. The safest lane is:
- “**Clinician-supervised decision support + documentation automation**.”

---

## Block 7 — Making money on X / TikTok / YouTube (faceless)
Yes. And your advantage is you have **a coherent doctrine** + **repeatable frameworks**.

### The content engine
**Format:** 30–60 second “protocol fragments” + 5–10 minute deeper dives  
**Faceless style:** slides, charts, on-screen text, B-roll, lab screenshots (de-identified), animated dashboards.

### Your best “content pillars” (high demand, low effort)
1) **Metabolic dashboard thinking** (glucose vs insulin vs A1c)
2) **Vitamin D fear dismantling** (with monitoring logic)
3) **Homocysteine explained simply** (thresholds + ladder)
4) **TG/HDL as metabolic signal**
5) **Diet ladder** (Lane B vs Lane N)
6) “Why your labs are ‘normal’ but you feel terrible” (people love this)

### Monetization ladder (clean and realistic)
1) Free content → trust
2) **Lead magnet**: “Clinic OS intake sheet + 4-month tracker” (PDF)
3) **Paid product**: templates pack / protocol library / prompt library
4) **Subscription**: “Clinic Brain updates” + new phenotypes monthly
5) **B2B**: license to clinics (highest revenue per customer)

**Do not** sell it as “cure X disease.” Sell it as:
- education
- clinical workflow
- decision-support templates
- coaching frameworks (if appropriate)

- **Rules decide the plan**
- **LLM writes it nicely**

This avoids hallucinations and keeps doctrine stable.

### Pattern C — Versioning is power
Every change becomes:
- v1 → v1.1 → v1.2
- changelog (“what changed and why”)

This is how you scale without chaos.

### 67. **ChatGPT:**

Yes. Now you’re describing a *real* app: not “an AI toy,” but a **patient-flow operating system** that mirrors your clinic end-to-end.

I’ll zoom out teleologically first (endpoints), then give you the **patient flow as modules**, then the **tools/steps to build** (MVP → v1 → v2), and I’ll annotate each section with **potential improvements** for later expansion.

---

## Teleology: what the app must achieve (true endpoints)

### Endpoint A — Clinical throughput without quality loss
- Patient arrives pre-structured (not “blank slate”)
- Labs are organized and machine-readable
- Interpretation is consistent with your doctrine
- Plan is generated fast, editable, versioned
- Follow-up is *inevitable* (compliance + monitoring loop)

**Metric:** time-to-plan drops massively; variance between doctors drops.

### Endpoint B — Patient adherence and clarity
- Patient gets a simple plan + why it matters
- They can report compliance + symptoms easily
- They know what’s “expected turbulence” vs red flags
- They show up for re-testing on schedule

**Metric:** fewer drop-offs; better follow-up completion.

### Endpoint C — A scalable product (internal → licensable)
- Your protocols become structured modules (rule engine)
- AI only writes, never decides dosing
- Supplements are pulled from your approved catalogs (NaturalDoctor + Meetab)
- Diet templates adapt but remain within allowed lanes

**Metric:** works for your clinic first; then for another clinician.

---

## The Patient Flow as an App (modules that match your real workflow)

Think of it as 7 stages with gates.

### Stage 0 — Pre-visit onboarding (before 1st appointment)
**Patient does:**
- fills general info
- uploads health files (optional)

**App does:**
- creates patient record
- tags uploaded files (labs, imaging, prescriptions, previous diagnoses)
- extracts key lab values when possible (or staff enters)

**Potential improvements**
- OCR / auto-parsing of PDF labs into structured values
- file type detection + auto-sorting (CBC, biochem, hormones, imaging)

---

### Stage 1 — Structured medical history + diet history + “metabolic typing”
**Patient does (or assistant helps):**
- medical history taking (structured form)
- metabolic typing (your prototype)
- diet history (your prototype)
- anthropometrics: height, weight, circumferences

**App does:**
- converts answers into phenotype tags (IR, gut, neuro, lipid, D, Hcy, etc.)
- shows clinician a “phenotype dashboard” before labs

**Potential improvements**
- risk flags (kidney stones, CKD, pregnancy, etc.)
- medication/supplement interaction warnings (rule-based)

---

### Stage 2 — Testing pipeline (metabolomics + fatty acids + extended biochem)
**Clinic does:**
- orders analytical testing:
  - organic acids / metabolomics (your system)
  - plasma free fatty acids
  - extended biochemical panel

**App does:**
- generates a “tests to order” checklist based on phenotype
- tracks status (ordered → collected → received)
- stores results as structured values + original PDFs

**Potential improvements**
- lab integration (API or semi-automated import)
- versioned “test bundles” (IR bundle, Gut bundle, Longevity bundle)

---

### Stage 3 — Interpretation engine (root problems + causal mapping)
**Clinician does:**
- interprets results; links to root problems

**App does (two-layer engine):**
1) **Rule engine (deterministic):**
   - triggers cornerstones based on thresholds/patterns
   - seen as “decision support,” not a black box
2) **LLM engine (language only):**
   - writes: patient summary, doctor note, regimen sheet
   - obeys your Clinic Brain prompt + “no invented doses”

**Potential improvements**
- causal graph view (root causes → downstream markers)
- “discordance resolver” (e.g., normal glucose + high insulin)

---

### Stage 4 — Intervention builder (supplements + diet templates → personalized plan)
**Clinician does:**
- selects protocol lanes (Diet Lane B vs Lane N)
- activates cornerstones (Vit D, Hcy, Gut, IR, Lipids, Foundation)
- edits regimen

**App does:**
- builds supplement plan from **approved catalogs**:
  - NaturalDoctor products
  - Meetab products
- attaches doses exactly from doctrine
- creates personalized diet plan using your prototypes + adaptations
- generates final artifacts:
  - 1-page patient plan
  - regimen sheet
  - follow-up tracker
  - doctor note

**Potential improvements**
- ingredient-based search (“needs magnesium glycinate 300 mg elemental”)
- automatic duplicate avoidance (same nutrient from multiple products)
- “budget mode” vs “optimal mode” regimen options

---

### Stage 5 — Follow-ups (compliance + symptom monitoring + expected ups/downs)
**Patient does:**
- logs adherence (diet + supplements)
- logs symptoms (energy, sleep, GI, cravings, etc.)
- sees reminders and education snippets

**Clinic does:**
- reviews compliance and adjusts levers
- documents “expected turbulence” vs “problem”

**App does:**
- shows compliance dashboard
- flags non-adherence risk
- generates a follow-up note template
- schedules next testing

**Potential improvements**
- streaks + simple behavior design (not gamified nonsense—clinical compliance)
- smart prompts: “if constipation ↑, check electrolytes + gut lane adjustments”

---

### Stage 6 — Re-evaluation timeline (4 / 8 / 16 / 28 months)
This is your long control loop.

**App does:**
- creates an automatic timeline per patient:
  - Month 4: re-test + adjust
  - Month 8: re-test + adjust
  - Month 16: re-test + adjust
  - Month 28: re-test + adjust
- stores “before vs after” dashboards
- generates progress report (“what changed, what remains”)

**Potential improvements**
- longitudinal graphs of key markers (insulin, A1c, Hcy, D, fatty acids)
- protocol version tracking: “what exactly were they on during each interval”

---

## The app architecture (so it’s expandable and safe)

### Two portals (minimum)
1) **Patient portal**
- onboarding forms
- uploads
- plan + education
- compliance tracking
- reminders

2) **Clinician portal**
- dashboards + phenotypes
- results view
- cornerstone activator
- regimen builder (supplements + diet templates)
- artifact generator
- follow-up + timeline

### Three engines under the hood
1) **Data model**: patients, labs, phenotypes, plans, versions  
2) **Rule engine**: thresholds → cornerstones → regimen skeleton  
3) **LLM writer**: turns skeleton into human documents

That’s how you scale to “more phenotypes/tests/protocols” without becoming a spaghetti monster.

---

## The exact steps you should take (practically)

### Step 1 — Freeze “v1 patient flow” as a PRD (product requirements doc)
You already have it; we just formalize it into:
- user stories (patient, assistant, doctor)
- screens
- required fields
- outputs
- security/GDPR needs

**Tool:** Obsidian (source of truth) + a PRD template.

### Step 2 — Build an internal MVP (fast) before anything public
Pick one build path:

**Fastest (low-code):**
- Bubble or Glide for UI + database
- Make/Zapier for automations
- LLM API for document writing
- PDF export tool

**Best if you have a dev:**
- Next.js frontend + Postgres
- File storage (S3-compatible)
- Role-based access
- LLM service with strict prompt + logging

### Step 3 — Ingest supplement catalogs (NaturalDoctor + Meetab) as structured data
You don’t “browse the site” inside the app; you maintain a catalog:
- product name, SKU, nutrients/ingredients, dose per unit, contraindications notes, price (optional)

**Tool options:**
- start with a CSV you curate manually (100–300 products)
- later: automated sync if feasible

### Step 4 — Convert your diets into templates + adaptation rules
- Lane B template
- Lane N template
- carb ladder rules
- exclusions (oxalates, legumes, seed oils, cow dairy)

### Step 5 — Pilot on 20 patients
- run onboarding → labs → plan → follow-ups
- note friction points
- release v1.1

# FILE — App PRD v1
**Filename:** `2026-01-18__App__ClinicOS_PRD__EN__v1`

## 1) Product definition
**ClinicOS** is a clinician-supervised platform that follows the entire patient journey:
**Pre-visit → history + metabolic typing → testing pipeline → interpretation → diet + supplements plan → follow-ups → re-evaluation at 4/8/16/28 months.**

Two principles:
- **Rules decide** (deterministic, auditable).
- **LLM writes** (communication + documentation only), strictly constrained by doctrine.

## 2) Primary users and jobs-to-be-done
### A) Patient
- Submit intake and files before first appointment
- Understand plan (diet + supplements + why)
- Track compliance and symptoms
- Show up for scheduled re-tests

### B) Clinic assistant / coordinator
- Ensure intake is complete
- Organize uploaded files
- Track test status (ordered → collected → received)
- Nudge compliance + schedule follow-ups

### C) Clinician (you / your doctors)
- Review phenotype + labs quickly
- Interpret using clinic doctrine
- Generate final plan artifacts fast
- Iterate plan based on compliance + re-testing

## 3) Success metrics
- Time from results received → finalized report: target **<15 min**
- Follow-up completion at month 4: target **>70%**
- Reduction in clinician variance: “same patient, similar output”
- Patient comprehension (simple survey): “I understand what to do and why”

## 4) Scope
### MVP (v1)
- Patient onboarding + upload
- Structured history + metabolic typing + diet history
- Anthropometrics
- Testing pipeline tracking
- Results storage (values + original files)
- Phenotype tags (manual + rule-based)
- Cornerstone activation + plan builder
- Supplements catalog (NaturalDoctor + Meetab) as internal database
- Diet templates (Lane B / Lane N + carb ladder)
- Follow-ups (compliance + symptom tracking)
- Re-test scheduling at **4/8/16/28 months**
- Artifact generation (patient summary, regimen, doctor note, follow-up tracker)

### v2 (later)
- Auto-parsing lab PDFs (semi-automatic)
- Longitudinal graphs + progress reports
- Advanced metabolomics modules (organic acids, custom biomarkers)
- Multi-clinic licensing features
- Patient “coach” chat layer (still supervised)

## 5) Patient flow mapped to screens (MVP)

### Stage 0 — Pre-visit onboarding
**Screen: Patient Signup & Consent**
- Identity, contact info
- Consent (GDPR), data usage
- Optional: “What are your top 3 goals?”

**Screen: Upload Health Files**
- Drag/drop PDFs/images
- Tags (optional by patient): “blood tests”, “imaging”, “diagnosis”, “meds”
- Staff can later re-tag

**Outputs**
- Patient record created
- File repository populated

---

### Stage 1 — Medical history + metabolic typing + diet history
**Screen: Medical History Form**
- Diagnoses, symptoms, family history
- Medications
- Allergies/intolerances
- Red flags / cautions (kidney stones, CKD, pregnancy etc.)

**Screen: Metabolic Typing (prototype)**
- Your existing questionnaire (as-is)

**Screen: Diet History (prototype)**
- Your existing diet history flow (as-is)

**Screen: Measurements**
- Height, weight
- Circumference(s): waist, hip, etc.

**Outputs**
- Phenotype tags preliminarily assigned (rule-based + clinician override)
- Baseline anthropometrics logged

---

### Stage 2 — Testing pipeline
**Screen: Recommended Tests**
- Clinician selects bundles:
  - Metabolomics (organic acids panel)
  - Free fatty acids panel
  - Extended biochem labs
- “Why this test” tooltip per bundle

**Screen: Test Status Tracker**
- Ordered → collected → received → interpreted
- Attach results PDF(s) when received
- Manual entry or import of values

**Outputs**
- Test orders recorded
- Results attached + structured where possible

---

### Stage 3 — Interpretation
**Screen: Results Dashboard**
- Tabs:
  - IR dashboard
  - Vit D dashboard
  - Homocysteine
  - Lipids / ApoB / fatty acids
  - Metabolomics panels (later: organic acids)
- Highlights: out-of-range vs clinic targets

**Screen: Root Problems Map**
- Clinician sees:
  - “Triggered cornerstones”
  - “Suspected root problems”
  - Explanation (auditable rules: “triggered because X”)

**Outputs**
- Cornerstones activated (with reasons)
- Draft plan skeleton generated (deterministic)

---

### Stage 4 — Intervention Builder (diet + supplements)
**Screen: Diet Plan Builder**
- Select Lane:
  - Lane B (base)
  - Lane N (keto)
- Plant toolkit checkboxes (standard)
- Carb ladder status (none / rice / bread / rare pasta)
- Dairy rule default (goat/sheep fermented; no cow except parmigiana)

**Screen: Supplements Builder**
- Adds cornerstone packs:
  - Foundation, VitD, Hcy, Gut, Lipid, etc.
- Pulls products from **NaturalDoctor catalog** + **Meetab catalog**
- Auto-checks for duplicates (e.g., Mg from 3 sources)
- Clinician edits final selection

**Outputs**
- Plan v1 created (versioned)
- Regimen items linked to products + doses

---

### Stage 5 — Follow-ups
**Screen: Patient Check-in**
- Compliance:
  - Supplements adherence %
  - Diet adherence %
- Weekly trackers:
  - energy (0–10), cravings (0–10), sleep (0–10)
  - stool frequency/form
  - bloating/reflux (0–10)
  - symptom notes

**Screen: Clinician Follow-up Review**
- Shows trends + adherence
- Suggests adjustments via doctrine lanes

**Outputs**
- Follow-up note template generated
- Plan updated to v1.1 if changes made

---

### Stage 6 — Re-evaluation scheduling
**Screen: Timeline**
- Milestones: **4 / 8 / 16 / 28 months**
- Each milestone includes:
  - tests to repeat
  - plan review
  - progress report output

**Outputs**
- Automated reminders
- Longitudinal comparisons (v2 adds graphs)

---

## 6) Artifacts generated (MVP)
- Patient Plan Summary (1 page)
- Regimen Sheet (supplements + diet lane + monitoring)
- Doctor Note (audit-friendly)
- Follow-up Tracker (weekly)
- Optional: relevant cornerstone leaflets / FAQs

## 7) Compliance and safety positioning
- App is **clinician-supervised decision support** + documentation automation.
- Patient-facing outputs are educational and procedural.
- Audit log required for plan changes.

# FILE — Data Schema v1
**Filename:** `2026-01-18__App__ClinicOS_DataSchema__EN__v1`

Below is a clean relational model that works in Postgres, Airtable, Glide, Bubble, Retool, etc.

## Core tables

### 1) Users
- `user_id` (PK)
- `role` (enum: patient, assistant, clinician, admin)
- `name`
- `email`
- `phone`
- `created_at`

### 2) Patients
- `patient_id` (PK)
- `user_id` (FK -> Users, nullable if patient not self-registered)
- `dob`
- `sex`
- `country`
- `consent_status` (enum)
- `created_at`

### 3) PatientFiles
- `file_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `uploaded_by_user_id` (FK)
- `file_type` (enum: lab_pdf, imaging, rx, note, other)
- `tag` (string)
- `storage_url`
- `uploaded_at`

### 4) IntakeSessions
- `intake_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `status` (draft, submitted, reviewed)
- `submitted_at`
- `reviewed_by_user_id` (FK)
- `reviewed_at`

### 5) IntakeAnswers
- `answer_id` (PK)
- `intake_id` (FK)
- `question_key` (string)
- `answer_value` (json/text)
- `created_at`

### 6) Measurements
- `measurement_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `date`
- `height_cm`
- `weight_kg`
- `waist_cm`
- `hip_cm`
- `notes`

### 7) Tests (orders)
- `test_order_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `bundle` (enum: metabolomics_OA, free_fatty_acids, extended_biochem, custom)
- `ordered_by_user_id` (FK)
- `status` (ordered, collected, received, interpreted, closed)
- `ordered_at`
- `received_at`

### 8) LabPanels
- `panel_id` (PK)
- `test_order_id` (FK)
- `panel_type` (enum: IR, VitD, Lipid, Homocysteine, CBC, Iron, Metabolomics_OA, FFA, Other)
- `collection_date`
- `lab_name`
- `source_file_id` (FK -> PatientFiles, nullable)

### 9) LabValues
- `value_id` (PK)
- `panel_id` (FK)
- `analyte` (string; e.g., fasting_insulin, homocysteine)
- `value` (numeric)
- `unit` (string)
- `reference_range` (text, optional)
- `flag` (low/normal/high, optional)
- `entered_by_user_id` (FK)
- `entered_at`

### 10) PhenotypeTags
- `tag_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `tag` (enum/string: IR, Gut, VitD, Lipid, Hcy, Neuro, Histamine, Constipation, Diarrhea, etc.)
- `source` (enum: intake_rule, lab_rule, clinician_manual)
- `confidence` (0–1)
- `created_at`

## Plan and versioning

### 11) Plans
- `plan_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `created_by_user_id` (FK)
- `active_plan_version_id` (FK -> PlanVersions)
- `created_at`

### 12) PlanVersions
- `plan_version_id` (PK)
- `plan_id` (FK)
- `version_label` (e.g., v1, v1.1)
- `cornerstones_activated` (json list)
- `diet_lane` (enum: lane_B, lane_N)
- `carb_ladder_step` (enum: none, rice, sourdough, pasta_rare)
- `notes_clinician` (text)
- `created_by_user_id` (FK)
- `created_at`

### 13) RegimenItems
- `regimen_item_id` (PK)
- `plan_version_id` (FK)
- `type` (enum: supplement, diet_rule, monitoring)
- `name` (string)
- `dose_text` (string)  # keep exact wording / “no drift”
- `schedule_text` (string)
- `source_cornerstone` (string)
- `product_id` (FK -> Products, nullable)
- `is_active` (bool)

## Supplement catalogs

### 14) Products
- `product_id` (PK)
- `vendor` (enum: naturaldoctor, meetab)
- `name`
- `sku` (optional)
- `url` (optional)
- `form` (capsule/powder/liquid/etc.)
- `serving_size_text`
- `ingredients` (json array)
- `nutrient_amounts` (json map; e.g., magnesium_elemental_mg: 100)
- `notes` (text)
- `active` (bool)

## Follow-ups and timeline

### 15) CheckIns
- `checkin_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `date`
- `supplement_adherence_percent`
- `diet_adherence_percent`
- `energy_0_10`
- `cravings_0_10`
- `sleep_0_10`
- `bloating_0_10`
- `reflux_0_10`
- `stool_notes`
- `free_text_notes`

### 16) Milestones
- `milestone_id` (PK)
- `patient_id` (FK)
- `month_number` (enum/int: 4, 8, 16, 28)
- `scheduled_date`
- `status` (upcoming, due, completed, skipped

Yes — you can “use all this” *as a system*, and yes, we can turn it into an app **and** a content engine. But first we need to **extract + structure** the supplement catalog so your protocols become computable.

Below is the clean way to think about it, plus what I can already pull from the two vendor sites, and the pipeline to pull the rest.

## Project index (files we are creating)
*(Copy/paste into Obsidian; we’ll keep appending.)*  
**2026-01-18 — AI Practice System**

## The core pattern: turn “supplements” into a database, then your protocols become an engine
Right now your knowledge is powerful but “text-shaped.”  
An app needs it “data-shaped.”

So we build a **Product Knowledge Layer**:

### A) Minimal data model (what every supplement becomes)
- **vendor** (NaturalDoctor / Meetab)
- **product_name**
- **sku / product_code**
- **form** (capsule / powder / liquid)
- **size** (caps count / grams / ml)
- **serving_size**
- **actives**: list of  
  - ingredient_name  
  - dose  
  - unit  
  - chemical_form (e.g., citrate, methylcobalamin)
- **other_ingredients** (excipients, flavors, capsule material)
- **directions**
- **warnings**
- **source_url**
- **label_image_url** (if the “Supplement Facts” are an image)
- **last_checked**

Once you have this, your protocol logic can do things like:
- compute daily totals (e.g., Mg elemental targets),
- avoid duplicates (two products both containing methylfolate),
- build “stacks” by phenotype,
- generate patient instructions automatically,
- track compliance and outcomes.

---

## What I can pull from the vendor sites (and what’s tricky)

### 1) NaturalDoctor.gr — **easy mode**
NaturalDoctor product pages include **ingredients as text** under **“Συστατικά”**, which is perfect for extraction and parsing.

Example (already extracted):

**NaturalDoctor — “B-Complex Active” (ingredients per daily dose / 1 capsule):**  
- Vitamin B1 (as thiamine HCl) — 50 mg  
- Vitamin B2 (as riboflavin) — 40 mg  
- Vitamin B3 (as nicotinamide) — 50 mg  
- Vitamin B5 (as calcium D-pantothenate) — 50 mg  
- Vitamin B6 (pyridoxal-5-phosphate) — 12 mg  
- Biotin (D-biotin) — 50 μg  
- Vitamin B12 (as methylcobalamin) — 50 μg  
- Folate (as L-methylfolate calcium) — 100 μg  
- Alfalfa (Medicago sativa) powder — 15 mg  
- Choline (as choline bitartrate) — 23 mg  
- Inositol (as myo-inositol) — 50 mg  
- PABA — 50 mg citeturn9view0turn9view1

Also: the “All products” page clearly lists many products with direct links, which is how we enumerate the full catalog. citeturn4view0turn6view3

**Obstacle:** direct automated scraping may be blocked depending on infrastructure, so the most reliable route is either:
- a negotiated **product feed/export** from them, or  
- scraping from a server/location they don’t block, while respecting robots/ToS.

### 2) Meetab.us — **medium-hard mode**
Meetab product pages often show “Formula and Ingredients” as a **label image** (Supplement Facts). Example: “My Calmag” links to an image containing the actual numbers. citeturn7view0turn11view0

Example (already extracted from the label image):

**Meetab — “My Calmag” (serving size 1/2 scoop, 1.2g):**  
- Vitamin D (as cholecalciferol) — 2,000 IU (50 mcg)  
- Calcium (from calcium citrate) — 78.1 mg  
- Magnesium (from magnesium citrate) — 91.8 mg  
Other ingredients: Natural lemon flavor, Stevia leaf extract. citeturn11view0

**Meetab — “My Probiotics” (serving size 1 capsule):**  
- Proprietary Probiotic Blend “60 Billion CFU Blend” — 200 mg  
  Includes: *L. casei, L. acidophilus, L. reuteri, L. rhamnosus, L. brevis, L. bulgaricus, B. bifidum, S. thermophilus, Lactococcus lactis, L. plantarum, L. paracasei, L. helveticus, L. keferi,* and other lactobacillus sub-species  
- L-Glutamine — 200 mg  
Other ingredients: Vegetable capsule (hydroxy-propyl-methylcellulose). citeturn12view0

**So Meetab requires OCR** (or vendor feed). The good news: label images are clean, so OCR is usually reliable.

---

## The extraction pipeline (what you actually do, step-by-step)

### Step 1 — Decide the scope (two modes)
- **Mode A (fast):** extract only the products you actually prescribe (build your clinical formulary first).  
- **Mode B (complete):** extract every product from both catalogs.

Clinically, Mode A is almost always smarter to start.

### Step 2 — Build two “connectors”
**Connector 1: NaturalDoctor**
1) Pull product URLs from “All products” list. citeturn4view0turn6view3  
2) For each product page, parse the “Συστατικά” bullet list into structured actives. citeturn9view0turn9view1  
3) Store as JSON/CSV.

**Connector 2: Meetab**
1) Pull product URLs from their “All supplements” listing (pagination exists). citeturn1view0turn4view1  
2) For each product page, find the label image linked in “FORMULA AND INGREDIENTS”. citeturn7view0  
3) Download label image.  
4) OCR it → parse into actives + other ingredients (usually printed clearly). citeturn11view0turn12view0  
5) Store as JSON/CSV.

### Step 3 — Normalize names (so your protocol engine doesn’t get stupid)
You will want a normalization table like:
- “Vitamin B12 (methylcobalamin)” = “cobalamin; methyl-”  
- “Magnesium (from magnesium citrate)” → magnesium salt, and optionally compute estimated elemental if stated elsewhere  
- “Folate (L-methylfolate calcium)” = “5-MTHF”

This is where your clinical precision becomes *software-grade precision*.

### Step 4 — Versioning
Every product gets:
- `last_checked`
- `vendor_version` (if available)
- diff tracking (“label changed since last sync”)

This matters because supplement companies quietly reformulate.

---

## Improvements to make this even better (you’ll thank yourself later)
### NaturalDoctor improvements
- Build a **“Clinical tags”** layer: `methylation`, `gut`, `insulin resistance`, `electrolytes`, `lipids`, `sleep`, etc.
- Add **contra / caution tags** per product (e.g., pregnancy, anticoagulants).

### Meetab improvements
- Request a **structured feed** (even a spreadsheet) from Meetab. OCR works, but feeds scale.
- Store the **label image** alongside the parsed text as the legal “ground truth.”

---

## Quick reality check: “Can I draw *all* supplements + ingredients?”
Yes, but *not manually* and not safely by copy/paste.

The correct way is:
- **ask vendors for a catalog export** (best), or  
- **build a crawler + OCR pipeline** (second best), or  
- start with **your clinical formulary** (fastest route to app + revenue).

---

## How this plugs into your app (the payoff)
Once products are structured, your app can:
- recommend stacks by phenotype (vitamin D / methylation / gut / insulin resistance),
- auto-generate the supplement plan with dosing + timing,
- warn about overlaps (double folate, too much zinc vs copper),
- schedule labs (25(OH)D, Ca, PTH; Hcy, B12/folate; etc.),
- generate follow-up questionnaires and compliance dashboards.

That’s how your “protocol philosophy” becomes a real clinical operating system.

---

### One clarification I *do* need (because it changes everything)
Do you want the first build to contain:
1) **Only the products you prescribe** (your clinic formulary, fast launch), or  
2) **The full NaturalDoctor + Meetab catalogs** (bigger project, slower, more maintenance)?

Either answer is fine — but it determines the first sprint and the architecture.

### 107. **ChatGPT:**

Perfect. You’re thinking like a systems architect now: **podcasts = raw training data**. NotebookLM becomes your “transcriber + librarian,” and your job is to ask it questions that force **structured extraction** instead of vibes.

Below is a **prompt pack** designed to turn 30 clinic podcasts into assets for **every arm** of the project:

- **App (patient flow + features + data model)**
- **Clinic doctrine (protocol library + triggers + dosing + monitoring)**
- **Catalog/formulary logic (NaturalDoctor + Meetab references)**
- **Training (doctor onboarding + scripts + SOPs)**
- **Media engine (faceless scripts, hooks, series, objections)**

I’ll give you:
1) A **workflow** (how to run the prompts in NotebookLM)
2) A **universal extraction schema** (so outputs are consistent)
3) The actual **copy-paste prompts** (modular)

---

## Workflow in NotebookLM (so you don’t drown)

### Pass 1 — Per podcast: produce a “Protocol Card”
Run prompts **P1 → P4** on each podcast and save outputs as separate notes.  
Naming convention: `Podcast_##__ProtocolCard`

### Pass 2 — Per podcast: produce “App Signals”
Run prompts **A1 → A3** on each podcast.  
Naming: `Podcast_##__AppSignals`

### Pass 3 — Per podcast: produce “Media Hooks”
Run prompts **M1 → M3** on each podcast.  
Naming: `Podcast_##__MediaHooks`

### Pass 4 — Cross-podcast synthesis
Run prompts **S1 → S4** across all sources.  
Naming: `Synthesis__v1`

This prevents the classic failure mode: one giant summary with no structure.

---

## Universal extraction schema (force structure)
Use this schema in prompts so the model outputs in a consistent format.

**Schema blocks**
- **Claims & Principles** (what the clinic believes)
- **Triggers** (when a protocol activates)
- **Targets** (numbers, ranges, goals)
- **Interventions** (diet + supplements + lifestyle if mentioned)
- **Dosing** (exact amounts; if not stated, mark as “not specified”)
- **Monitoring cadence** (what labs, how often)
- **Stop rules / safety** (when to pause, reduce, investigate)
- **Phenotypes** (subtypes, special cases, decision forks)
- **Products mentioned** (NaturalDoctor / Meetab names, ingredients)
- **Patient communication** (best metaphors, phrases, objection handling)
- **Uncertainties / TODOs** (what is implied but not defined)
- **Quotable lines** (for media)

---

# PROMPT PACK (copy/paste)

## P1 — Protocol Card (core extraction, per podcast)
Paste this into NotebookLM after selecting a single podcast source:

**Prompt:**
> Create a “Protocol Card” from this podcast using the exact headings below.  
> Important: do NOT invent numbers. If a dose/range/cadence is not explicitly stated, write “NOT SPECIFIED.”  
> If a concept is repeated, merge it into one clean statement.  
>
> **1) Title + 1-sentence thesis**  
> **2) Core principles (clinic doctrine claims)**  
> **3) Phenotypes/subtypes discussed**  
> **4) Triggers (what activates intervention)**  
> **5) Targets (explicit lab/symptom targets, include units)**  
> **6) Interventions**  
> - Diet interventions  
> - Supplement interventions  
> - Other interventions (if any)  
> **7) Dosing table (only explicit numbers)**  
> **8) Monitoring cadence & labs**  
> **9) Stop rules / safety constraints**  
> **10) Contraindications / caution populations**  
> **11) Patient messaging (metaphors, calming frames, objections + answers)**  
> **12) Product mentions (NaturalDoctor / Meetab; list product names + what they’re used for)**  
> **13) Open questions / TODOs (what would need clarification to operationalize this in an app)**  
>
> End with: **“Key quotes”** (up to 10 short quotes/paraphrases, not long).

---

## P2 — Numbers & thresholds extraction (make the app computable)
**Prompt:**
> Extract every explicit numeric threshold, target range, dose, frequency, timeline, and lab cadence mentioned in the podcast.  
> Output as a list of JSON objects with these fields:  
> `{ "parameter": "", "value": "", "unit": "", "context": "", "trigger_condition": "", "monitoring": "", "source_phrase": "" }`  
> Do not infer missing numbers.

---

## P3 — Decision forks (phenotype logic)
**Prompt:**
> Identify all “if X then Y” decision rules in the podcast (even informal ones).  
> Output as bullet rules in this structure:  
> - IF [condition] THEN [action] BECAUSE [reason]  
> Mark any missing definitions as TODO.  
> Do not invent medical device-like certainty; keep it as clinic logic.

---

## P4 — Safety & malpractice-proofing
**Prompt:**
> Extract every safety-related statement: monitoring labs, toxicity risks, red flags, “when to stop,” and caution groups.  
> Then propose a “Safety Checklist v0.1” that the app could show clinicians BEFORE finalizing a plan.  
> Only use content from the podcast; do not add external facts.

---

# APP-SPECIFIC PROMPTS

## A1 — Patient journey mapping (your exact flow)
**Prompt:**
> Map everything in this podcast to the patient journey stages below.  
> For each stage, list what data is collected, what decisions are made, and what outputs are produced.  
>
> Stages:  
> 0) Pre-visit onboarding + uploads  
> 1) Medical history + metabolic typing + diet history + measurements  
> 2) Testing pipeline (metabolomics, free fatty acids, extended biochem)  
> 3) Interpretation (root problems)  
> 4) Intervention builder (diet templates + supplements)  
> 5) Follow-ups (compliance + ups/downs)  
> 6) Re-evaluation timeline (4/8/16/28 months)  
>
> Output format: Stage → Inputs → Decisions → Outputs → App UI needs → TODOs.

---

## A2 — Data model extraction (what tables/fields you’ll need)
**Prompt:**
> Based on this podcast, list the data entities the app must store.  
> Output as:  
> - Entity name  
> - Required fields  
> - Optional fields  
> - Relations (which entity links to which)  
>  
> Examples of entities: PhenotypeTag, LabValue, DietTemplate, RegimenItem, Product, Contraindication, FollowUpCheckIn, Milestone.

---

## A3 — Artifact generator requirements (what documents must be produced)
**Prompt:**
> From this podcast, infer what written artifacts the clinic needs to generate.  
> Output as: Artifact → Purpose → Required sections → Required data inputs → Tone (patient/doctor/staff).  
> Only use what the podcast implies.

---

# FORMULARY / CATALOG PROMPTS (NaturalDoctor + Meetab)

## F1 — Product mention extractor (per podcast)
**Prompt:**
> Extract every supplement/product mentioned by name (brand + product) and categorize by purpose.  
> Output as a table-like list:  
> - Product name (as spoken)  
> - Brand/vendor (NaturalDoctor / Meetab / other / unknown)  
> - Intended use / protocol pillar  
> - Any dosing mentioned (exact only)  
> - Any ingredient forms mentioned (e.g., methylcobalamin, citrate)  
> - Notes/TODO (if name unclear)

## F2 — Ingredient/form extraction (standardize)
**Prompt:**
> Extract all mentions of nutrient forms and ingredient preferences (e.g., “methylfolate,” “methylcobalamin,” “magnesium citrate/threonate,” “butyrate form,” etc.).  
> Output as: Ingredient → Preferred forms → Avoided forms → Rationale → Where used (which protocol).

---

# MEDIA ENGINE PROMPTS (faceless X / TikTok / YouTube)

## M1 — Hook library (short-form)
**Prompt:**
> Create 20 short hooks (1 sentence each) based strictly on this podcast.  
> Each hook must point to a clear concept like “normal glucose but high insulin,” “vitamin D safety loop,” “homocysteine ladder,” etc.  
> No medical cure claims. Education framing only.

## M2 — 10 faceless shorts scripts (30–60 sec)
**Prompt:**
> Write 10 faceless short-video scripts (30–60 sec) from this podcast.  
> Each script must include:  
> - Hook (1 line)  
> - Core explanation (3–5 lines)  
> - One metaphor (dashboard/thermostat/repair mode)  
> - Soft CTA: “talk to your clinician / get labs / learn the framework”  
> Avoid absolute promises or disease claims.

## M3 — Objection handling clips (high conversion)
**Prompt:**
> List the top objections/fears mentioned or implied in the podcast (at least 10).  
> For each: write a 15-second response suitable for a faceless video.  
> Tone: calm, confident, non-combative.

---

## T2 — Staff SOP extraction
**Prompt:**
> Extract operational steps mentioned (how to take history, how to order tests, how to follow up, how to explain results).  
> Convert into a clinic SOP checklist that staff can follow.

### 108. **Simos:**

P1 

Ακολουθεί η «Κάρτα Πρωτοκόλλου» (Protocol Card) που βασίζεται στις πηγές και στις αρχές της Μεταβολομικής Ιατρικής:

### **Κάρτα Πρωτοκόλλου: Μεταβολομική Ιατρική & Βιταμίνη D**

**1) Τίτλος + Θέση 1 πρότασης**
**Πρωτόκολλο Αποκατάστασης της Βιοχημικής Ισορροπίας και Ανοσορύθμισης.**
Η υγεία επιτυγχάνεται μέσω της διόρθωσης των ελλείψεων σε κυτταρικό επίπεδο και της αποκατάστασης των φυσιολογικών μεταβολικών διεργασιών, με κεντρικό πυλώνα τη βιταμίνη D [1-3].

**2) Βασικές αρχές (Clinic Doctrine)**
*   Το σώμα έχει μια **έμφυτη τάση προς την αυτοίαση** (οργάνωση ενάντια στην εντροπία) [4-6].
*   Η ιατρική είναι επιστήμη και τέχνη: απαιτεί **εξατομίκευση** της γνώσης για κάθε μοναδικό ασθενή [7-9].
*   Η **Βιταμίνη D λειτουργεί ως ορμόνη** που «ξεκλειδώνει» χιλιάδες γονίδια απαραίτητα για την επιδιόρθωση των ιστών [2, 10, 11].
*   Τα θρεπτικά συστατικά δρουν **συνεργικά**: η έλλειψη ενός συμπαράγοντα μπορεί να μπλοκάρει ολόκληρα μεταβολικά μονοπάτια [12-14].

**3) Φαινότυποι / Υπότυποι**
*   **Αυτοάνοσα νοσήματα:** (Χασιμότο, Σκλήρυνση κατά πλάκας, Ρευματοειδής Αρθρίτιδα, Ψωρίαση, Λεύκη) [15, 16].
*   **Μεταβολικό Σύνδρομο:** Αντίσταση στην ινσουλίνη, παχυσαρκία, υπέρταση [17-19].
*   **Αντίσταση στη Βιταμίνη D:** Άτομα με δυσλειτουργία υποδοχέων που απαιτούν πολύ υψηλές δόσεις για βιολογικό αποτέλεσμα [20-23].
*   **Χρόνια Φλεγμονή:** Ασθενείς που δεν μπορούν να ολοκληρώσουν τη διαδικασία επούλωσης [24-26].

**4) Εναύσματα (Triggers)**
*   **Μεταβολικό Στρες:** Έλλειψη ενέργειας (ATP) λόγω ελλείψεων σε βιταμίνες και μέταλλα [27-29].
*   **Δυτική Διατροφή:** Υπερ-επεξεργασμένες τροφές, ζάχαρη και σπορέλαια [30-32].
*   **Δυσβίωση & Διαπερατό Έντερο:** Πέρασμα τοξινών στην κυκλοφορία που «τυφλώνει» το ανοσοποιητικό [33-35].
*   **Ορμονικές μεταβολές:** Εγκυμοσύνη, εμμηνόπαυση, εφηβεία [13, 36, 37].

**5) Στόχοι (Targets)**
*   **25(OH)D3 (Αίμα):** >50 ng/ml (πρόληψη), 70-100 ng/ml ή και >100 ng/ml (αυτοάνοσα) [38-41].
*   **Παραθορμόνη (PTH):** Στο κατώτερο φυσιολογικό όριο (δείκτης επάρκειας βιολογικής δράσης D) [42-45].
*   **Ινσουλίνη Νηστείας:** 3-6 μIU/ml (ιδανικό) [46].
*   **Γλυκόζη Νηστείας:** 75-85 mg/dl (ιδανικό), <100 mg/dl (φυσιολογικό) [47, 48].
*   **HbA1c (Γλυκοζυλιωμένη):** <5,6% [49].
*   **Λόγος LDL / ApoB:** >1,2 (δείκτης μεγάλων και υγιών σωματιδίων) [50, 51].

**6) Παρεμβάσεις**
*   **Διατροφικές:** Κατανάλωση πλήρων τροφών (κρέας μηρυκαστικών, αυγά, κατσικίσια γαλακτοκομικά, θαλασσινά) [52-54]. Απομάκρυνση ζάχαρης, αλευριού και βιομηχανικών ελαίων [31, 32, 55].
*   **Συμπληρώματα:** Φυσική D3 (χοληκαλσιφερόλη) με **Μαγνήσιο, Κ2, Ψευδάργυρο και Βόριο** [12, 56, 57]. Πολυβιταμίνη με **μεθυλοφολικό** και **μεθυλοκοβαλαμίνη** [58-60].
*   **Άλλες:** Περπάτημα σε εξωτερικό χώρο (ρύθμιση νευροδιαβιβαστών), έκθεση στον ήλιο, ύπνος πριν τις 22:30 [61-64].

**7) Πίνακας Δοσολογίας**
*   **Βιταμίνη D3 (Ασφαλής δόση):** 5.000 - 10.000 IU / ημέρα [56, 65].
*   **Βιταμίνη D3 (Υψηλή θεραπευτική):** >10.000 IU, έως 50.000 - 70.000 IU (ΜΟΝΟ υπό ιατρική επίβλεψη) [15, 52, 66].
*   **Πρωτεΐνη (Πρωινό):** 40 g (για διακοπή καταβολισμού) [67-69].
*   **Νερό:** 2 - 3,5 L ημερησίως (ανάλογα με το βάρος) [70-72].
*   ** Brazil Nuts (για Σελήνιο):** 3-4 καρποί / ημέρα [57].

**8) Συχνότητα παρακολούθησης & Εξετάσεις**
*   **Μεταβολομικές Αναλύσεις:** 3 φορές το πρώτο οκτάμηνο (έναρξη, 4ος μήνας, 8ος μήνας). Στη συνέχεια ετησίως ή ανά διετία [73-75].
*   **Εργαστηριακά:** 25(OH)D3, PTH, Ασβέστιο, Ινσουλίνη νηστείας, HbA1c, LDL/ApoB, Τριγλυκερίδια [41, 50, 76-78].
*   **Απεικονιστικά:** Calcium Score (κάθε 1-2 έτη για εκτίμηση αθηρωμάτωσης) [79, 80].

**9) Κανόνες διακοπής / Περιορισμοί ασφαλείας**
*   **Φυσική D3:** Πρακτικά αδύνατη η τοξικότητα· το σώμα μετατρέπει την περίσσεια σε αδρανείς μεταβολίτες [7, 81, 82].
*   **Φαρμακευτική D (Καλσιτριόλη):** Στενό όριο ασφαλείας· κίνδυνος υπερασβεστιαιμίας [7, 83-85].
*   **Calcium Score:** Αν αυξηθεί πάνω από 5% μεταξύ μετρήσεων, η αθηρωματική πλάκα θεωρείται ενεργή [86, 87].

**10) Αντενδείξεις / Πληθυσμοί με προσοχή**
*   **Νεφρική Ανεπάρκεια:** Απαιτεί φαρμακευτικές (ενεργοποιημένες) μορφές βιταμίνης D λόγω αδυναμίας ενεργοποίησης [85, 88-90].
*   **Γυναίκες & Διαλειμματική Νηστεία:** Μπορεί να αυξήσει την κορτιζόλη και να διαταράξει τις ορμόνες φύλου· προτείνεται σποραδική χρήση [91-93].
*   **Νεφρολιθίαση (Οξαλικά):** Περιορισμός σε σπανάκι, αμύγδαλα, παντζάρια, κακάο [94-97].

**11) Μηνύματα προς τον ασθενή**
*   **Μεταφορές:** Η βιταμίνη D είναι η «πόρτα»· οι υπόλοιπες βιταμίνες είναι το «μαγείρεμα» μέσα στην κουζίνα [42, 98].
*   **Καθησυχασμός:** Η ιατρική είναι ανθρωποκεντρική· το DNA δεν είναι η μοίρα σας, η επιγενετική καθορίζει το 75-80% [99-101].
*   **Αντιρρήσεις:** «Το κρέας κάνει κακό;» - Το κόκκινο κρέας μηρυκαστικών είναι η πιο θρεπτική και αντιφλεγμονώδης τροφή [52, 102, 103].

**12) Αναφορές προϊόντων**
*   ** Meetab / Natural Doctor:** Συμπληρώματα χωρίς τοξικά έκδοχα (τιτάνιο, αλουμίνιο, talc) που απευθύνονται σε συνολικά μεταβολικά μονοπάτια [104-107].
*   **Ενεργές μορφές:** Μεθυλοφολικό (ενεργή Β9) και Μεθυλοκοβαλαμίνη (ενεργή Β12) για άμεση απορρόφηση [58-60, 108].

**13) Ανοιχτά ερωτήματα TODO**
*   Περαιτέρω διερεύνηση της αναστροφής αθηρωματικών πλακών μέσω συνδυασμού Νατοκινάσης και βιταμίνης Κ2 [109].
*   Ανάγκη για κλινικά δεδομένα σχετικά με τη δράση και των 92 μεταλλικών στοιχείων του φυσικού αλατιού [110].
*   Εξατομίκευση του «ιδανικού» μικροβιώματος με βάση τη γεωγραφική προέλευση [111, 112].

---

## 2. QC AUDIT — where you violated the rules (important)

Now the hard part.  
Remember the rule from the prompt:

> **“Do NOT invent numbers. If not explicitly stated, mark NOT SPECIFIED.”**

You violated this in several places. This does **not** make the protocol wrong — but it makes it **non-computable** and **legally risky** for an app.

I’ll mark issues by severity.

---

### 🔴 HIGH SEVERITY (must be fixed before app use)

#### 1. Targets that may not be explicitly stated in the podcast
Examples:
- `25(OH)D >50, 70–100, >100`
- `Ινσουλίνη 3–6 μIU/ml`
- `Γλυκόζη 75–85 mg/dl`
- `HbA1c <5.6`
- `LDL/ApoB >1.2`

These **may be correct clinically**, but unless the **podcast explicitly said these numbers**, they must be tagged as:

- `EXPLICIT (spoken)`
- or `CLINIC STANDARD (not stated here)`

👉 **Fix:**  
Add a tag per target:
- `[EXPLICIT – Podcast]`
- `[CLINIC STANDARD – Derived]`

The app will later treat these differently.

---

#### 2. Dosing ranges without explicit attribution
Examples:
- `D3 50,000–70,000 IU`
- `Protein 40g breakfast`
- `Water 2–3.5 L`
- `Brazil nuts 3–4`

Unless the speaker **said these exact numbers**, they must be flagged.

👉 **Fix:**  
In dosing tables, add a column:

| Intervention | Dose | Status |
|--------------|------|--------|
| Vitamin D3 | 10,000 IU | EXPLICIT |
| Vitamin D3 | 50,000 IU | CLINIC PRACTICE (NOT STATED) |

This matters enormously for medico-legal safety.

---

### 🟠 MEDIUM SEVERITY (needs clarification, not deletion)

#### 3. Strong claims without qualifiers
Examples:
- “Πρακτικά αδύνατη η τοξικότητα”
- “Αναστροφή αθηρωματικών πλακών”
- “DNA is not destiny 75–80%”

These are **excellent for podcasts**, but in an app they must be framed as:

- educational
- theory-based
- clinician-supervised

👉 **Fix:**  
Add a label:
- `Educational framing`
- `Working clinical theory`
- `Observed in practice`

We are building a **decision-support system**, not a manifesto.

---

### 🟡 LOW SEVERITY (philosophical, but keep)

These are fine and valuable:
- entropy vs self-organization
- epigenetics framing
- metaphors
- patient reassurance language

These belong in:
- **Patient Messaging Layer**
- **Media Engine**
- **Doctor training**

Not in the **rule engine**.
